*hold¹
/həʊld ||; hold/verb (past tense past participle held /held ||; hɛld/)
1 [T] to take sb/sth and keep him/her/it in your hand, etc 拿着；握着；抱着: He held a gun in his hand. 他手中拿着枪。 The woman was holding a baby in her arms. 那个妇人怀中抱着婴儿。 Hold my hand. This is a busy road. 这条路车子多，拉着我别放手。 ☞picture on page S19 见S19页插图
2 [T] to keep sth in a certain position 使保持在某个位置上: Hold your head up straight. 把头抬直。 Hold the camera still or you'll spoil the picture. 端稳相机别动，要不然会拍坏的。 These two screws hold the shelf in place. 这两枚螺钉把架子固定住。
3 [T] to take the weight of sb/sth 承受得住…的重量: Are you sure that branch is strong enough to hold you? 你敢肯定那树枝够结实，承受得住你的重量？
4 [T] to organize an event; to have a meeting, an election, a concert, etc 筹办（活动）；举行（会议、选举、音乐会等）: They're holding a party for his fortieth birthday. 他们要举办一个酒会，为他庆祝四十岁生日。 The Olympic Games are held every four years. 奥运会每四年举行一次。
5 [I] to stay the same 持续；维持: I hope this weather holds till the weekend. 我希望这样的天气能一直维持到周末。 What I said still holds -- nothing has changed. 我说过的仍算数，什么也没改变。
6 [I,T] to contain or have space for a particular amount 容纳；装得下: The car holds five people. 这辆汽车坐得下五个人。 How much does this bottle hold? 这个瓶子容量多少？
7 [T] to keep a person in a position or place by force 用武力迫使某人留在某位置或地方: The terrorists are holding three men hostage. 恐怖分子目前把三个男子扣为人质。 A man is being held at the police station. 有个男人被拘押在警察局里。
8 [T] to have sth, usually in an official way 持有: Does she hold a British passport? 她是不是持英国护照？ She holds the world record in the 100 metres. 她保持着100米短跑的世界纪录。
9 [T] to have an opinion, etc 抱有（见解等）: They hold the view that we shouldn't spend any more money. 他们认为，我们不该再花钱了。
10 [T] to believe that sth is true about a person 认为: I hold the parents responsiblefor the child's behaviour. 我认为父母应对儿女的行为负责任。
11 [I,T] (used when you are telephoning) to wait until the person you are calling is ready （用于打电话时）不挂断（等对方接听） · I'm afraid his phone is engaged. Will you hold the line ? 他的电话恐怕占线，请你等一等，别把电话挂掉。
12 [T] to have a conversation 进行谈话: It's impossible to hold a conversation with all this noise. 这么吵嚷，无法谈话。
Hold it!(spoken 口语) Stop! Don't move! 站住！别动！ For other idioms containing hold, look at the entries for the nouns, adjectives, etc. For example hold your own is at own. 其他含hold的习语，参看有关名词、形容词等词条，如hold your own可参看词条own。 hold sth against sb to not forgive sb because of sth he/she has done （由于某人做了某事而）不原谅某人 hold sb/sth back
1 to prevent sb from making progress 阻碍
2 to prevent sb/sth from moving forward 阻止…前进: The police tried to hold the crowd back. 警察努力把群众挡住。
hold sth back
1 to refuse to give some of the information that you have 有所隐瞒；保守秘密: The police are sure that she is holding something back. She knows much more than she is saying. 警方认为她必定隐瞒着什么，她知道的远远不止她说出来的事情。
2 to control an emotion and stop yourself from showing what you really feel 抑制，控制（感情）: He fought to hold back tears of anger and frustration. 他拚命忍住愤怒和沮丧的眼泪。
hold off (sth/doing sth) to delay sth 推迟；拖延 hold on
1 to wait or stop for a moment 等候或停下片刻: Hold on. I'll be with you in a minute. 等一等，我马上就来。
2 to manage in a difficult or dangerous situation 在困难或危险的情况下坚持下去: They managed to hold on until a rescue party arrived. 他们成功地坚持到救援人员到达。
hold onto sb/sth to hold sb/sth tightly 紧紧抓住: The child held on to his mother; he didn't want her to go. 小孩紧抓着他妈妈，不让她走开。 hold onto sth to keep sth; to not give or sell sth 保留；不给；不卖: They've offered me a lot of money for this painting, but I'm going to hold onto it. 他们出高价要买这幅画，但我不会卖。 hold out to last (in a difficult situation) （在困境中）维持，坚持: How long will our supply of water hold out? 我们的水够用多久？ hold sth out to offer sth by moving it towards sb in your hand 把（某物）递给某人: He held out a carrot to the horse. 他把胡萝卜递给马吃。 hold out for sth(informal 非正式) to cause a delay while you continue to ask for sth 坚持要求；不达要求不罢休: Union members are holding out for a better pay offer. 工会成员坚决要求提高工资。 hold sb/sth up to make sb/sth late; to cause a delay 阻延；造成阻延: We were held up by the traffic. 路上车多使我们耽误了。 hold up sth to rob a bank, shop, vehicle, etc using a gun （持枪）抢劫（银行、商店、车辆等）
hold²
/həʊld ||; hold/noun
1 [C] the act or manner of having sb/sth in your hand(s) 抓；拿；握: to have a firm hold on the rope 抓紧绳子 judo/wrestling holds 柔道╱摔跤擒拿法
2 [sing] a hold (on/over sb/sth) influence or control 影响；控制: The new government has strengthened its hold on the country. 新政府对全国加强了控制。
3 [C] the part of a ship or an aircraft where cargo is carried （船或飞机的）货舱 ☞picture at plane 见plane插图
catch, get, grab, take, etc hold (of sb/sth)
1 to take sb/sth in your hands 用手抓住╱拿住╱握住…: I managed to catch hold of the dog before it ran out into the road. 狗还来不及跑到马路上，我就捉住了它。
2 to take control of sb/sth; to start to have an effect on sb/sth 控制；开始影响: Mass hysteria seemed to have taken hold of the crowd. 群众的情绪似乎都很激动。
get hold of sb to find sb or make contact with sb 找到；跟…联络上: I've been trying to get hold of the complaints department all morning. 整个早上我都在设法跟申诉部门联络。 get hold of sth to find sth that will be useful 找到（日后有用的东西）: I must try and get hold of a good second-hand bicycle. 我得弄一辆好的二手自行车。

*hole
/həʊl ||; hol/noun

3 [C] (in golf) the hole in the ground that you must hit the ball into. Each section of the land where you play(golf course)is also called a hole. （高尔夫球）球洞，球穴区: an eighteen-hole golf course 十八个洞的高尔夫球场

*holiday
/ˈhɒlədeɪ ||; ˈhɑləˌde/noun
1 (US 美 vacation) [C,U] a period of rest from work or school (often when you go and stay away from home) 假期（常指离家的）: We're going to Italy for our summer holidaysthis year. 今年我们要去意大利过暑假。 How much holiday do you get a year in your new job? 你的新工作每年给多少天假期？ Mr Philips isn't here this week. He's away on holiday. 这个星期菲利普斯先生不在这里，他度假去了。 I'm going to take a week's holidayin May and spend it at home. 我打算在五月休假一个礼拜，呆在家里不出门。 the school/Christmas/Easter/summer holidays 学校假期；圣诞节假期；复活节假期；暑假
Leave is time when you do not go to work for a special reason sick leave maternity leave (= when you are having a baby) unpaid leave 因某种特殊理由而请的假叫做leave﹕sick leave病假?maternity leave产假?unpaid leave无薪假期
2 [C] a day of rest when people do not go to work, school, etc often for religious or national celebrations 假日（常因宗教或国家的庆祝活动）: Next Monday is a holiday. 下星期一是假日。 New Year's Day is a bank/public holiday in Britain. 元旦是英国的银行╱公共假日。
Holiday in this sense is used in both British and American English. A day when you choose not go to work is also called a day off I'm having two days off next week when we move house. 就这个意义来说，holiday一词英美通用。休假一天也叫做a day off：I'm having two days off next week when we move house.下个礼拜我请了两天假搬家。

*home¹
/həʊm ||; hom/noun
1 [C,U] the place where you live or where you feel that you belong 家: She left home (= left her parents' house and began an independent life) at the age of 21. 她21岁那年离家，开始过独立生活。 Children from broken homes (= whose parents are divorced) sometimes have learning difficulties. 破碎家庭的儿童有时在学习上会遇到困难。 That old house would make an ideal family home. 那座老房子不失为一个理想的居所。 ☞ Look at the note at house. 参看house的注释。
Be careful. The preposition to is not used before ‘home ’ It's time to go home. She's usually tired when she gets/arrives home. If you want to talk about somebody else's home you have to say at Jane and Andy's or at Jane and Andy's place/house. 注意：home一词前面不可用介词to：It's time to go home.是该回家的时候了。·She's usually tired when she gets／arrives home.她回到家里的时候，通常很疲倦。谈及别人的家，得说at Jane and Andy's或 at Jane and Andy's place／house，两句均指在珍妮和安迪两人的家里。
2 [C] a place that provides care for a particular type of person or for animals 对某类人或动物提供照顾的地方: a children's home (= for children who have no parents to look after them) 儿童收容所 an old people's home 养老院
3 [sing] the home of sth the place where sth began 发源地；发祥地: Greece is said to be the home of democracy. 希腊被誉为民主的发源地。
at home
1 in your house, flat, etc 在家: Is anybody at home? 有人在家吗？ Tomorrow we're staying at home all day. 明天我们不出门，整天在家。
In American English home is often used without the preposition at Is anybody home? 美国英语里，home往往不与介词at连用：Is anybody home?有人在家吗？
2 comfortable, as if you were in your own home 无拘束；自在；就像在自己家里一样: Please make yourself at home. 请别拘束。 I felt quite at home on the ship. 我觉得在船上相当自在。
3 (used in sport) played in the town to which the team belongs （体育）在主场: Manchester City are playing at home on Saturday. 曼彻斯特城队星期六将在主场比赛。

*honest
/ˈɒnɪst ||; ˈɑnɪst/adj
1 (used about a person) telling the truth; not lying to people or stealing （指人）诚实的: Just be honest -- do you like this skirt or not? 说老实话，你喜欢不喜欢这条裙子？ To be honest, I don't think that's a very good idea. 老实说，我认为这不是个很好的主意。
2 showing honest qualities 显示诚实的: an honest face 诚实的面孔 I'd like your honest opinion, please. 有意见，只管直说。 [OPP] for both senses dishonest 两个义项的反义词皆为dishonest ➔honesty noun [U] [OPP] dishonesty 反义词为dishonesty

honestly
/ˈɒnɪstli ||; ˈɑnɪstlɪ/adv
1 in an honest way 诚实地: He tried to answer the lawyer's questions honestly. 他试图老老实实地回答律师的问题。
2 used for emphasizing that what you are saying is true （用于强调说的是实话）: I honestly don't know where she has gone. 我真的不知道她去了哪儿。
3 used for expressing disapproval （用于表示不满）: Honestly! What a mess! 哎！真是一团糟！

2 a word for ‘darling’, used especially in American English 亲爱的，宝贝（在美国尤为常用）

honorary
/ˈɒnərəri; US ˈɒnərerɪ ||; ˈɑnəˌrɛrɪ/adj
1 given as an honour (without the person needing the usual certificates, etc) 作为荣誉而授予的（接受者无须具备有关资历）: to be awarded an honorary degree 被授予名誉学位
2 oftenHonorary(abbr Hon) not paid 名誉的；无报酬的: He is the Honorary President. 他是名誉主席。

*honour¹
/ˈɒnə(r) ||; ˈɑnɚ/ (US 美 honor) noun
1 [U] the respect from other people that a person, country, etc gets because of high standards of behaviour and moral character 崇敬；尊敬: the guest of honour(= the most important one) 贵宾 ☞Look at dishonour. 参看dishonour。
2 [sing] (formal 正式) something that gives pride or pleasure 光荣: It was a great honour to be asked to speak at the conference. 承蒙邀请在会上致辞，深感荣幸。
3 [U] the quality of doing what is morally right 名誉；声誉: I give you my word of honour. 我用名誉作担保。
4 Honours [pl] the four highest marks you can be given in Bachelor degrees 荣誉学位
5 [C] something that is given to a person officially, to show great respect 表示荣誉、尊敬而正式授予之物或仪式: He was buried with full military honours(= with a military ceremony as a sign of respect). 他下葬时举行了隆重的军葬礼。
in honour of sb/sth;in sb/sth's honour out of respect for sb/sth 为了向…表示敬意: A party was given in honour of the guests from Bonn. 为来自波恩的宾客举行了酒会。
honour²
/ˈɒnə(r) ||; ˈɑnɚ/ (US 美 honor) verb [T]
1 honour sb/sth (with sth) to show great (public) respect for sb/sth or to give sb pride or pleasure 向…表示敬意: I am very honoured by the confidence you have shown in me. 承蒙器重，不胜荣幸。
2 to do what you have agreed or promised 实践或履行诺言

*hook¹
/hʊk ||; hυk/noun[C]
1 a curved piece of metal, plastic, etc that is used for hanging sth on or for catching fish 钩；鱼钩: Put your coat on the hook over there. 把你的外套挂在那边的钩子上。 a fish-hook 鱼钩
2 (used in boxing) a way of hitting sb that is done with the arm bent （拳击比赛）钩拳: a right hook (= with the right arm) 右钩拳
off the hook (used about the top part of a telephone) not in position, so that telephone calls cannot be received （指电话听筒）没有挂好（因此电话打不进来） get/let sb off the hook(informal 非正式) to free yourself or sb else from a difficult situation or punishment 使摆脱困境或惩罚: My father paid the money I owed and got me off the hook. 爸爸帮我还了债，为我解了围。
hook²
/hʊk ||; hυk/verb
1 [I,T] to fasten or catch sth with a hook or sth in the shape of a hook; to be fastened in this way （被或用钩）钩；（被或用钩状物）钩（住） · We hooked the trailer to the back of the car. 我们将拖车钩在汽车后面。 The curtain simply hooks onto the rail. 窗帘给栏杆钩住了。
2 [T] to put sth through a hole in sth else （将某物）穿过…: Hook the rope through your belt. 将绳子从你的皮带穿过去。
hook (sth) up (to sth) to connect sb/sth to a piece of electronic equipment or to a power supply 将…接上电子设备或电源

hop¹
/hɒp ||; hɑp/verb [I] (hopping; hopped)
1 (used about a person) to jump on one leg （指人）单足跳跃: I had twisted my ankle so badly I had to hop all the way back to the car. 我的脚踝严重扭伤，我不得不单足跳回到汽车那里。
2 (used about an animal or bird) to jump with both or all feet together （指鸟兽）齐足跳跃
3 hop (from sth to sth) to change quickly from one activity or subject to another 从一个活动或话题迅速转到另一个活动或话题
hop it!(slang 俚语) Go away! 滚开！ hop in/into sth;hop out/out of sth(informal 非正式) to get in or out of a car, etc (quickly) （快速）上或下汽车等 hop on/onto sth;hop off sth(informal 非正式) to get onto/off a bus, etc (quickly) （快速）上╱下公共汽车等

/hɒp ||; hɑp/noun

2 [C] a tall climbing plant with flowers 啤酒花藤，忽布（一种攀爬植物）

*hope¹
/həʊp ||; hop/verb [I,T] hope that...;hope to do sth;hope (for sth) to want sth to happen or be true 希望（某事发生或成真） [I] ‘Is it raining?’ ‘ I hope not. I haven't got a coat with me.’ “在下雨吗？”“希望不是。我没带雨衣呢。” [I] ‘Are you coming to London with us ?’ ‘I'm not sure yet but I hope so.’ “你会与我们一起到伦敦来吗？”“有这个想法，不过还说不准。” I hope that you feel better soon. 希望你早日好转。 Hoping to hear from you soon (= at the end of a letter). 伫候回音（写于信末）。
*hope²
/həʊp ||; hop/noun
1 [C,U] (a) hope (of/for sth);(a) hope of doing sth;(a) hope that... the feeling of wanting sth to happen and thinking that it will 希望: What hope is there for the future? 未来还有什么希望？ There is no hope of finding anybody else alive. 再没有希望找到其他生还者了。 David has high hopes of becoming a jockey (= is very confident about it). 戴维对成为骑师充满信心。· She never gave up hope that a cure for the disease would be found. 她坚信总有一天能找到治愈这种疾病的方法。
2 [sing] a person, a thing or a situation that will help you get what you want 带来希望的人、事物或情况: Please can you help me? You're my last hope. 求你帮帮我，你是我最后的指望了。
dash sb's hopes (of sth/of doing sth)→DASH² in the hope of sth/that… because you want sth to happen 抱着…的希望: I came here in the hope that we could talk privately. 我到这里来，是想跟你单独谈谈。 pin (all) your hopes on sb/sth→PIN² a ray of hope→RAY

/ˈhəʊpfl ||; ˈhopfəl/adj

*hospital
/ˈhɒspɪtl ||; ˈhɑspɪtḷ/noun [C] a place where ill or injured people are treated 医院: He was rushed to hospital in an ambulance. 救护车赶紧把他送到医院去。 to be admitted to/discharged from hospital 入院／出院 a psychiatric/mental hospital 精神病医院 If a person goes to hospital or is in hospital (without ‘the’), he/she is a patient receiving treatment there His mother's in hospital. She cut her hand and had to go to hospital. ‘The hospital’ refers to one particular hospital, or indicates that the person is only visiting the building temporarily He went to the hospital to visit Muriel. to hospital或in hospital（没有the）表示病人在医院接受治疗：His mother's in hospital.他的母亲住院了。·She cut her hand and had to go to hospital.她手割伤了，不得不去医院就医。the hospital指某家医院或者表示某人只是暂时去那个建筑物：He went to the hospital to visit Muriel.他去医院看望缪里尔。 A person who is being treated in a hospital by doctors and nurses is a patient. If you have an accident you are taken first to the casualty department (US emergency room). 在医院里受到医生(doctor)和护士(nurse)照料的病人叫patient。遇到事故就先送到急诊室(casualty department)（美国英语叫emergency room）。
hospitality
/ˌhɒspɪˈtæləti ||; ˌhɑspɪˈtælətɪ/noun [U] looking after guests and being friendly and welcoming towards them 好客；殷勤款待

*host
/həʊst ||; host/noun[C]
1 a person who invites guests to his/her house, etc and provides them with food, drink, etc 主人；东道主 ☞Look at hostess. 参看hostess。
2 a person who introduces a television or radio show and talks to the guests （电视或电台的）节目主持人
3 a host of sth a large number of people or things 一大群或许多（人或事物）
4 an animal or a plant on which another animal or plant lives and feeds 寄主，宿主（被其他动物或植物寄生的动物或植物） host verb · The city is aiming to host the Olympic Games in ten years' time. 该市争取在十年后主办奥林匹克运动会。

*hostage
/ˈhɒstɪdʒ ||; ˈhɑstɪdʒ/noun [C] a person who is caught and kept prisoner. A hostage may be killed or injured if the person who is holding him/her does not get what he/she is asking for 人质: The robbers tried to take the staff hostage. 那几个盗贼试图把全体员工扣作人质。 The hijackers say they will hold the passengers hostageuntil their demands are met. 劫机者说，他们要挟持乘客作为人质，直到他们的要求得到满足。 ☞Look at ransom. 参看ransom。

/ˈhɒstl ||; ˈhɑstḷ/noun[C]

2 a building where people who have no home can stay for a short time （无家可归的人的）收容所

hostile
/ˈhɒstaɪl; US -tl ||; ˈhɑstḷ/adj hostile (to/towards sb/sth) having very strong feelings against sb/sth 怀有敌意的；敌视的: a hostile crowd 怀有敌意的群众 They are very hostile to any change. 他们非常反对任何变革。

hostility
/hɒˈstɪləti ||; hɑsˈtɪlətɪ/noun
1 [U] hostility (to/towards sth) very strong feelings against sb/sth 敌意；敌视: She didn't say anything but I could sense her hostility. 她什么也没有说，可是我感受到她的敌意。 [SYN] animosity 同义词为animosity
2 hostilities [pl] fighting in a war 战事

*hot¹
/hɒt ||; hɑt/adj (hotter;hottest)
1 having a high temperature 热的: Can I open the window? I'm really hot. 我可不可以打开窗子？我热得很。 It was boiling hot on the beach. 海滩上热得不得了。 a hot meal 一顿热饭 Don't touch the plates -- they're red hot ! 别碰这些盘子，十分烫手的！
You can describe the temperature of sth as freezing (cold), cold, cool, tepid (used about water), warm, hot or boiling (hot). 形容东西的温度，可以用freezing (cold)（冰冷）、cold（冷）、cool（凉）、tepid（不冷不热）（指水）、warm（暖）、hot（热）或boiling (hot)（滚热）。 ☞Look also at the note at cold ¹. 另参看cold^1的注释。
2 (used about food) causing a burning feeling in your mouth （指食物）辣的: hot curry 辣咖喱 [SYN] spicy 同义词为spicy
3 (informal 非正式) difficult or dangerous to deal with 对付起来很难或很危险: The defenders found the Italian strikers too hot to handle. 防守队员觉得很难抵御意大利前锋的进攻。
4 (informal 非正式) exciting and popular 热门的；极风行的: This band is hot stuff ! 这支乐队现在红得发紫！
in hot pursuit following sb who is moving fast 穷追不舍

*hour
/ˈaʊə(r) ||; aυr/noun
1 [C] a period of 60 minutes 小时；钟头: He studies for three hoursmost evenings. 大多数夜晚他要学习三个小时。 The programme lasts about half an hour. 那个节目长半小时。 I'm going shopping now. I'll be back in about an hour. 我要去买些东西，大约一个钟头后回来。 In two hours' timeI'll be having lunch. 我两个钟头后吃中饭。 a four-hour journey 四个小时的路程 Japan is eight hours ahead of the UK. 日本比英国早八个小时。 I get paid by the hour. 我是按钟点计酬的。 How much do you get paid per/an hour ? 你的时薪多少？
2 [C] the distance that you can travel in about 60 minutes 一小时行程: London is only two hours away. 去伦敦只要两个小时。
3 hours [pl] the period of time when sb is working or a shop, etc is open 工作时间；营业时间: Employees are demanding shorter working hours. 雇员要求缩短工作时间。
4 [C] a period of about an hour when sth particular happens 约一小时的时间: I'm going shopping in my lunch hour. 午饭时候，我要去买东西。 The traffic is very bad in the rush hour. 上下班的时候交通很混乱。
5 the hour [sing] the time when a new hour starts (= 1 o'clock, 2 o'clock, etc) …点钟: Buses are on the hour and at twenty past the hour. 公共汽车在每个钟头正点及其后二十分开出一班。
6 hours [pl] a long time 长时间: He went on speaking for hours and hours. 他不停地讲了很长很长时间。
at/till all hours at/until any time 在╱到任何时候: She stays out till all hours (= very late). 她很晚才回来。 the early hours→EARLY

hourly
/ˈaʊəli ||; ˈaυrlɪ/adj adv
1 done, happening, etc every hour 每小时一次: an hourly news bulletin 每小时一次的新闻简报 Trains are hourly. 火车每小时开出一趟。
2 for one hour 以钟点计算: What is your hourly rate of pay? 你的时薪多少？

*house¹
/haʊs ||; haυs/noun [C] (plural houses /ˈhaʊzɪz ||; ˈhaυzɪz/)
1 a building that is made for people to live in 房屋；住宅: Is yours a four-bedroomed or a three-bedroomed house? 你们的房子是四间卧室的还是三间卧室的？ ☞ Look at bungalow, cottage and flat. 参看bungalow、cottage及flat。
Your home is the place where you live, even if it is not a house Let's go home to my flat. Your home is also the place where you feel that you belong. A house is just a building We've only just moved into our new house and it doesn't feel like home yet. 居所即使不是房子都叫home：Let's go home to my flat.我们回我的公寓去吧。home也指给人归属感的地方。house只是一座建筑物：We've only just moved into our house and it doesn't feel like home yet.我们刚刚搬到新房子去，感觉还不像一个家。 You can build, do up, redecorate or extend a house. You may rent a house from somebody or let it out to somebody else. If you want to move house you go to an estate agent. 房子可以盖(build)、装修(do up)、重新装潢(redecorate)或扩建(extend)，也可以租用(rent)或租出(let)。要是想搬家(move house)，可以去找房地产经纪(estate agent)。
2 [usu.sing] all the people who live in one house 住在同一房子里的所有人: Don't shout. You'll wake the whole house up. 别喊，要不然准把全家吵醒。
3 a building that is used for a particular purpose （作特定用途的）建筑物: a warehouse 仓库
4 a large firm involved in a particular kind of business 商业机构；公司: a fashion/publishing house 时装公司；出版社
5 a restaurant, usually that sells one particular type of food 饭店（尤指出售某类食品的）: a curry/spaghetti house 咖喱菜饭店；意大利面条店 house wine (= the cheapest wine on a restaurant's menu) 饭店里最便宜的酒
6 House a group of people who meet to make a country's laws 议院: the House of Commons 下议院 the Houses of Parliament 国会两院 ☞Look at the note at Parliament. 参看Parliament的注释。
7 [usu.sing] the audience at a theatre or cinema, or the area where they sit （剧院或电影院里的）观众，观众席: There was a full house for the play this evening. 今天晚上这场戏客满。
move house→MOVE¹ on the house paid for by the pub, restaurant, etc that you are visiting; free 由酒馆或餐馆等支付费用；免费: Your first drink is on the house. 头一杯饮品是免费的。 get on/along like a house on fire to immediately become good friends with sb （跟某人）很快成为好友

*how
/haʊ ||; haυ/adv conj
1 (often used in questions) in what way （常用于疑问句）以什么方式，怎样: How do you spell your name? 你的名字是怎么拼的？ Can you show me how to use this machine? 可以给我介绍一下这台机器的用法吗？ I can't remember how to get there. 我记不得去那儿的路了。
2 used when you are asking about sb's health or feelings （用于询问健康状况或感觉）: ‘How is your mother?’ ‘She's much better, thank you.’ “你妈妈怎么样？”“好多了，谢谢你的关心。” How are you feeling today? 你今天感觉怎么样？ How do you feel about your son joining the army? 你对自己的儿子参军有什么看法？
You use ‘how’ only when you are asking about a person's health. When you are asking about a person's character or appearance you say what ... like ? ‘What is your mother like? ’ ‘Well, she's much taller than me and she's got dark hair.’ 询问健康状况用how﹔询问某人的性格或外表可以用what... like﹕‘What is your mother like?'‘Well, she's much taller than me and she's got dark hair.'“你妈妈是什么样子的﹖”“好呀﹐个子比我高得多﹐长一头黑色的头发。”
3 used when you are asking about sb's opinion of a thing or a situation （用于询问对事情或情况的看法）: How was the weather? 天气怎么样？ How is your meal? 那顿饭吃得如何？ How did the interview go? 面试进行得怎么样？
4 used in questions when you are asking about the degree, amount, age, etc of sb/sth （用于疑问句，询问程度、数量、年纪等）: How old are you? 你多大年纪？ How much is that? 那个多少钱？
5 used for expressing surprise, pleasure, etc （表示惊讶、喜悦等）多么，何等: She's gone. How strange! 她走了。真奇怪！ I can't believe how expensive it is! 那么贵，我简直无法相信。
how/what about...?→ABOUT² how come?→COME how do you do?(formal 正式) used when meeting sb for the first time （初次见面时的问候语）您好 Be careful. How are you? and How do you do? are answered differently. ‘How do you do?’ is answered with the same words ‘How do you do?’ The answer to ‘How are you?’ depends on how you are feeling ‘I'm fine.’/‘Very well.’/‘Much better.’ 注意：回答How are you?跟How do you do?并不相同：对方说How do you do?就应回答说How do you do?对方说How are you?就可视乎情况而回答说I'm fine.我精神不错。／Very well.我精神很好。／Much better.我好多了。
*however
/haʊˈevə(r) ||; haυˈɛvɚ/adv conj
1 (formal 正式) (used for adding a comment to what you have just said) although sth is true （用于补充刚说过的话）可是，然而: Sales are poor this month. There may, however, be an increase before Christmas. 这个月的销售量很不理想。不过，圣诞节之前也许会增长。
2 (used in questions for expressing surprise) in what way; how （用于疑问句，表示惊奇）到底以什么方式，究竟怎样: However did you manage to find me here? 你到底怎么知道我在这儿？ ☞ When you use only how in a question like this there is not such a feeling of surprise. 这类问句要是只用how，惊奇的语气就会减弱。
3 in whatever way 不管用什么方式或方法: However I sat I couldn't get comfortable. 我怎么坐也不舒服。 You can dress however you like. 你爱穿什么就穿什么。
4 (before an adjective or adverb 用于形容词或副词前) to whatever degree 不管什么程度: He won't wear a hat however cold it is. 不管天气怎么冷，他也不戴帽子。 You can't catch her however fast you run. 你跑得多快也追不上她。

*hunger¹
/ˈhʌŋgə(r) ||; ˈhʌŋgɚ/noun
1 [U] the state of not having enough food to eat, especially when this causes illness or death 饥饿: In the Third World many people die of hunger each year. 第三世界每年都有许多人饿死。 ☞Look at thirst. 参看thirst。
2 [U] the feeling caused by a need to eat 饿: Hunger is one reason why babies cry. 肚子饿是婴儿啼哭的原因之一。
Be careful. You cannot say I have hunger in English. You must say: I am hungry. 注意：“我肚子饿”不能说I have hunger，应该说I am hungry。
3 [sing] a hunger (for sth) a strong desire for sth 渴望: a hunger for knowledge/fame/success 对知识╱名气╱成功的渴求

*hurry¹
/ˈhʌri ||; ˈhʌrɪ/noun [U] the need or wish to do sth quickly 急忙；匆忙: Take your time. There's no hurry. 慢慢来，别着急。 in a hurry quickly 急忙: She got up late and left in a hurry. 她起床起得晚，匆忙出门去了。 in a hurry (to do sth) wanting to do sth soon; impatient 急于（做某事）: They are in a hurry to get the job done before the winter. 他们要赶在冬天来临之前把这件事完成。 in no hurry (to do sth);not in any hurry (to do sth)
1 not needing or wishing to do sth quickly 不急于（做某事）: We weren't in any hurry so we stopped to admire the view. 我们有的是工夫，所以停下来欣赏一下景色。
2 not wanting to do sth 不想或不愿意（做某事）: I am in no hurry to repeat that experience. 我才不想重蹈覆辙呢。
*hurry²
/ˈhʌri ||; ˈhʌrɪ/verb (present participle hurrying third person singular present hurries;past tense past participle hurried)
1 [I] to move or do sth quickly because there is not much time 急忙行动或做某事: Don't hurry. There's plenty of time. 别急，时间多着呢。 They hurried back home after school. 他们一下课就赶紧回家。 Several people hurried to help. 有几个人赶来帮忙。
2 hurry sb (into sth/doing sth) [T] to cause sb/sth to do sth, or sth to happen more quickly 催促: Don't hurry me. I'm going as fast as I can. 别催我，我已经尽量快了。 He was hurried into a decision. 他在催促下作出决定。
3 [T] (usually passive 通常用于被动语态) to do sth too quickly 仓促进行
hurry up (with sth)(informal 非正式) to move or do sth more quickly 赶紧行动或做某事: Hurry up or we'll miss the train. 快点，要不就赶不上火车了。

*hurt¹
/hɜ:t ||; hɝt/verb (past tense past participle hurt)
1 [T] [I] to cause sb/yourself physical pain or injury 弄痛；使受伤: Did he hurt himself? 他把自己弄伤了吗？ I fell and hurt my arm. 我栽了一跤，伤了胳膊。 No one was seriously hurt in the accident. 这次事故中没有人受重伤。 These shoes hurt; they're too tight. 这双鞋太紧了，脚都穿痛了。
Compare hurt, injure and wound. A person may be wounded by a knife, sword, gun, etc, usually as a result of fighting a wounded soldier. People are usually injured in an accident Five people were killed in the crash and twelve others were injured. Hurt and injured are similar in meaning but hurt is more often used when the damage is not very great I hurt my leg when I fell off my bike. 比较hurt、injure及wound。受刀伤、剑伤、枪伤等都叫wounded，通常是打斗所致：a wounded soldier伤兵。在事故里受伤通常叫injured：Five people were killed in the crash and twelve others were injured.撞车事故里有五人死亡，十二人受伤。hurt和injured的意思相近，但hurt一般用于不大严重的伤势：I hurt my leg when I fell off my bike.我骑自行车的时候掉了下来，摔伤了腿。
2 [I] to feel painful 产生疼痛的感觉: My leg hurts. 我的腿痛。 It hurts when I lift my leg. 我的腿一提起来就痛。 Where exactly does it hurt? 到底是哪个部位痛？
3 [T] to make sb unhappy; to upset sb 使伤心；使烦恼: His unkind remarks hurt her deeply. 他那些无情的话伤透了她的心。 I didn't want to hurt his feelings. 我不想伤害他的感情。
it won't/wouldn't hurt (sb/sth) (to do sth)(informal 非正式) used to say that sb should do sth （表示某人应该做某事）…也无妨: It wouldn't hurt you to help with the housework occasionally. 你有时帮忙做点家务也无妨。
*hurt²
/hɜ:t ||; hɝt/adj
1 injured physically 受伤的: None of the passengers were badly/seriously hurt. 旅客当中无人严重受伤。
2 upset and offended by sth that sb has said or done 伤心的: She was deeply hurt that she had not been invited to the party. 她没有被邀请参加舞会，感到很伤心。
hurt³
/hɜ:t ||; hɝt/noun [U] a feeling of unhappiness because sb has been unkind or unfair to you （精神上的）痛苦，创伤: There was hurt and real anger in her voice. 从她说话的口气听得出她很痛苦，而且确实很生气。

hurtful
/ˈhɜ:tfl ||; ˈhɝtfəl/adj hurtful (to sb) unkind; making sb feel upset and offended 刻薄的；伤感情的

hurtle

*husband

hypocrite
/ˈhɪpəkrɪt ||; ˈhɪpəˌkrɪt/noun [C] a person who pretends to have moral standards or opinions which he/she does not really have. Hypocrites say one thing and do another 虚伪的人；伪君子: What a hypocrite! She says she's against the hunting of animals but she's wearing a fur coat. 好一个伪君子！她嘴上说反对捕猎动物，身上却穿着毛皮大衣。 ➔hypocritical /ˌhɪpəˈkrɪtɪkl ||; ˌhɪpəˈkrɪtɪkḷ/ adj ➔hypocritically /-kli ||; -klɪ/ adv

/haɪˈpɒθəsɪs ||; haɪˈpɑθəsɪs/noun [C] (plural hypotheses /-si:z ||; -ˌsiz/) an idea that is suggested as the possible explanation for sth but has not yet been found to be true or correct 假说（对客观事物的假定说明）；假设

hypothetical
/ˌhaɪpəˈθetɪkl ||; ˌhaɪpəˈθɛtɪkḷ/adj based on situations that have not yet happened, not on facts 假定的；假设的: That's a hypothetical question because we don't know what the situation will be next year. 这只是一个假设的问题，因为我们不知道来年的情况。 ➔hypothetically /-kli ||; -klɪ/ adv

hysteria
/hɪˈstɪəriə ||; hɪsˈtɪrɪə/noun [U] a state in which a person or a group of people cannot control their emotions, for example cannot stop laughing, crying, shouting, etc 歇斯底里病； 癔病；情绪激动: mass hysteria 群情鼎沸

hysterical
/hɪˈsterɪkl ||; hɪsˈtɛrɪkḷ/adj
1 very excited and unable to control your emotions 歇斯底里的: hysterical laughter 狂笑 She was hysterical with grief. 她伤心过度而歇斯底里。
2 (informal 非正式) very funny 十分滑稽的 ➔hysterically /-kli ||; -klɪ/ adv

hysterics
/hɪˈsterɪks ||; hɪsˈtɛrɪks/noun[pl]
1 an expression of extreme fear, excitement or anger that makes sb lose control of his/her emotions 歇斯底里的状态（因极其恐惧、激动或愤怒而情绪失控）: She went into hysterics when they told her the news. 他们告诉她这个消息时，她就陷入歇斯底里了。 (informal 非正式) My father would have hysterics (= be furious) if he knew I was going out with you. 我爸爸要是知道我跟你相好，一定会大发雷霆。
2 (informal 非正式) laughter that you cannot control 狂笑: The comedian had the audience in hysterics. 那位喜剧演员逗得观众笑个不停。
